# Source classification backfill preview, 2026-05-11

READ-ONLY heuristic backfill for the 783 sources currently NULL on `source_role`. Applies the 5-axis framework at `docs/source-classification-framework-2026-05-10.md`. NO DATABASE WRITES. Operator approves batches before any UPDATE executes.

## TL;DR

- Total scope: 783 sources
- HIGH confidence: 398 (51%)
- MEDIUM confidence: 122 (16%)
- LOW confidence: 224 (29%)
- AMBIGUOUS (human review required): 39
- URL-split-flagged sources (review for splitting before any batch executes): 11
- Total batches: 8 batches sorted by item-count DESC

## Methodology

Per-source proposal derived from five signals, weighted as follows:

1. **Host pattern + URL match** (primary). Built from framework worked examples plus role inclusion rules. Match against `name + url + description` haystack. First match wins. HOST_RULES table covers ~120 known patterns: regulator domains (`.gov`, `.gov.uk`, `europa.eu`), IGO domains (`imo.org`, `icao.int`, `iea.org`), standards bodies, statistical agencies (`bls.gov`, `eia.gov`, `eurostat`), academic (`.edu`, `.ac.[cc]`, national labs, peer-reviewed journals), industry data providers (`bloomberg(nef)`, `msci`, `argusmedia`), trade press (`freightwaves`, `joc`, `lloydslist`), industry associations (`iata`, `bimco`, `iru`, vertical-specific GCC/albert/Julies Bicycle), vendor corporate (`maersk`, `boeing`, `dhl`).
2. **Existing `sources.tier`** (integer 1-7 per migration 004). Reused as-is, never overridden. Tier-fallback assigns role when no host rule matches: tier 1-2 = primary_legal_authority, tier 3 = academic_research, tier 4 = statistical_data_agency, tier 5 = trade_press, tier 6 = industry_data_provider, tier 7 = trade_press but flagged AMBIGUOUS per framework Section 2.
3. **Item-type distribution per source** queried from `intelligence_items.item_type`. With 5+ items, used as a confirmation or conflict signal. Confirmation boost: regulator with >40% regs, data provider with >50% market data, academic with >40% research, standards with >30% standards. Conflict downgrade: trade_press with >50% regs (review for primary_legal_authority); primary_legal_authority with >60% market data (review for industry_data_provider).
4. **Name-pattern conflict detection**. Flags AMBIGUOUS when name carries a strong signal (Alliance/Coalition/Association/Federation, University/College, Think Tank/Institute, corporate suffix, news/journal/magazine) that contradicts the host-derived role.
5. **Existing legacy fields** (`intelligence_types`, `domains[]`, `transport_modes`) selected but not yet woven into the rules. Listed for future refinement; today the heuristic is mostly host + name + tier + item-history.

Default expected_output distributions per role: midpoint of framework Axis 5 ranges. Stored as JSONB shape `{Regulatory, Research, Market_Intel, Operations, Out_of_Scope}` summing to 1.0.

**Confidence definitions:**
- **HIGH**: exact framework worked-example match OR clear domain match (e.g., `freightwaves.com` matches the trade_press table) AND item history confirms or no item history conflict.
- **MEDIUM**: clear name-pattern + item-type alignment (e.g., name contains 'EFRAG', item history is research-heavy). Or HIGH downgraded because no item history exists yet.
- **LOW**: tier fallback only, no host pattern matched, no item history. Single weak signal.
- **AMBIGUOUS**: signals conflict (host suggests trade_press but >50% items are regs), or multiple roles plausible (corporate suffix in name when role is academic_research), or framework-flagged anomaly (tier 7 legacy outlier). **Human review required before backfill executes.**

## URL-split-flagged sources, need human review before any batch executes


## Methodology caveats

**Heuristic, not deterministic.** This backfill applies pattern matching, not the full framework decision logic. Caveats by category:

- **`.gov` over-broad**: Generic `.gov` pattern catches all US federal regulators by default. State-level governments (Colorado, Missouri, etc.) get jurisdiction `us-state` via the explicit state-legislature rule, but the `.gov` fallback assigns `us-federal` for state agency domains we didn't enumerate. Operator should spot-check state-vs-federal jurisdiction in the LOW confidence rows.
- **EU member-state regulators**: Domains like `.de`, `.fr`, `.es` get `eu` jurisdiction by default. If member-state granularity matters (`eu-de`, `eu-fr`), human pass needed.
- **Vertical detection is name-only**: Vertical assignment (`fine_art`, `live_events`, etc.) only fires when name keyword matches. Many sources default to `freight_general` even when their actual vertical is, e.g., humanitarian. Operator pass per role can refine.
- **Modes default to `none`**: Sources without explicit mode keywords (air/ocean/road/rail) get `none`. Many regulators DO cover transport without saying so in their name. Operator pass per regulator domain can refine.
- **Tier reuse, never override**: The script reuses `sources.tier` integer as-is. Per framework Section 2 schema-mapping note, framework values T1-T6 = integer 1-6. The 20 tier-7 legacy outliers are flagged AMBIGUOUS and do NOT receive the framework's six-tier assignment until human review.
- **Multi-role only as fallback**: Per framework, multi-role single-source is the fallback. URL-pattern split is preferred. The URL-split-flagged section at the top lists candidates. Today's backfill assigns single role only; secondary_roles is left as `[]`. Splits are operator decisions.
- **Item-type history is shallow**: 596 of 783 sources have at least 1 item; 187 have zero. Sources with zero items get the host-pattern proposal with the no-history downgrade applied (HIGH becomes MEDIUM). Sources with 1-4 items get the proposal but item-type signal is too thin to confirm or conflict.
- **Expected output is the framework default per role**: Per framework Axis 5, observed history will refine these distributions after 30-90 days of ingestion. For now every same-role source shares the same default distribution. Drift detection per framework Section 5b applies once observed_distribution accumulates.

**Where assignments may need human override** (not exhaustive):
- Generic `.gov` matches that should be statistical_data_agency (hits beyond bls/eia/census not enumerated)
- Generic `.edu` matches that should be vendor (corporate research arm publishing through a `.edu`-affiliated channel)
- Trade press hosted on regulator-adjacent domains (e.g., a regulator-published newsletter on a `.gov` subdomain)
- Industry associations with `.gov` or `.org` domains where the host rule didn't recognize them (only top-tier associations are in HOST_RULES)
- Vertical-specific sources (fine_art, live_events, film_tv, automotive, humanitarian) outside the explicit vertical-keyword set

**Re-run instructions for the executor:**
Operator approves a batch verbally. Executor copies the corresponding SQL Batch N block, opens a Supabase SQL editor, and runs the BEGIN ... COMMIT block. The `WHERE source_role IS NULL` guard ensures idempotency. After every batch, executor verifies the row count of `sources WHERE source_role IS NOT NULL` increased by the expected amount.

End preview.
